FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT
- Please call [PHONE-41] to make and/or confirm your follow-up appointment. BRAIN SURGERY INCISION CARE
- Wash your hair and gently massage the incision daily with baby shampoo. - Do not use any creams or ointments. - Do not blow dry, color or chemically treat your hair for at least 6 months. DISCHARGE ACTIVITY
- Do not drive or operate dangerous equipment within 24 hours of using pain meds. - If you have had seizures, do not drive or operate dangerous equipment until cleared by your surgeon. - No lifting > 10 lbs. (i.e. one gallon of milk) or strenuous activity until cleared by your surgeon. - Light walking is encouraged
- If you were issued a cervical collar, then wear it at all times
- If you were issued a back brace, then wear it when sitting up greater than 45 degrees or standing
DISCHARGE DIET
- Low sugar diet (No simple sugars, fruit juices, sweetened beverages, sweets made with sugar) while on
steroids.- Vitamin C supplement over the counter (500 mg daily for 30 days, 250 mg daily thereafter), if you are a
current or recent smoker. DISCHARGE MEDICATIONS
- The nurses will give you a list of your new medications and home medication to resume. - A limited supply of pain medication will be provided by your surgeon Take only as needed. Pain medication
refills will only be considered by your surgeon after you have been seen on your scheduled routine follow-up visit. I
have counseled the patient on the risks and benefits of narcotic use and patient has verbalized understanding. - Prescription refills are completed during normal weekday office hours only. CALL THE OFFICE AT [PHONE-42] FOR:

Fluids/Drains: None
Indications: Daniel W Volk is a 58 yr/o male who presented with imaging 
demonstrated right parietal lobe mass. I had a detailed conversation with the
patient and family regarding potential benefits, risks and alternative to the
procedure listed above. They consented to the procedure. Operation: The patient was positively identified and marked in the preoperative
holding room. He was transferred to the operating room and placed under
general endotracheal anesthesia. All appropriate monitoring devices were
placed. The patient was then positioned in the Mayfield pin head holder. All
pressure points were adequately padded. The stereotactic navigation system
was then registered to the patient's head and utilized to plan an incision and
craniotomy. DVT prophylaxis was provided. Preoperative antibiotics were
administered. The patient's head was prepped with alcohol followed by
chlorhexidine followed by ChloraPrep solution and draped in sterile fashion. A
preoperative timeout was performed.
The location of the incision was confirmed again with the stereotactic navigation
system. Local anesthetic was administered. Using a 10 blade scalpel incision
was fashioned. Hemostasis was obtained utilizing Raney clips and bipolar
electrocautery. The scalp was retracted in a subperiosteal fashion. Using the
stereotactic navigation system to confirm the appropriate location of burr holes
and using the Midas drill we fashioned a craniotomy without complication. The
bone dust was washed away with copious amounts of antibiotic irrigation. Hemostasis was obtained along the bone edges with bone wax and thrombin- soaked Gelfoam. We then brought the stereotactic navigation system back into
the field to confirm the extent of the bony exposure. The ultrasound was used to
further confirm the exposure.
Next the dura was incised and reflected to expose the underlying brain. We again
interrogated lesion with the ultrasound. At this point the microscope was brought
into the field and the resection of the lesion was performed under microscope
Generated on 12/6/23 1:25 PM Page 66

magnification utilizing microsurgical dissection technique. Utilizing tumor
forceps, Rhoton dissectors and cottonoids, we worked circumferentially around
the margin of the lesion. Hemostasis was obtained with bipolar electrocautery
and thrombin-soaked cotton sponges. As we identified the tumor margin, we
debulked the lesion internally. The capsule was then dissected further off of the
brain and folded inward. We used the stereotactic navigation system as well as
ultrasound throughout the extent of the resection for guidance. When satisfied with the extent of resection we turned our attention to hemostasis
which was obtained utilizing bipolar electrocautery, Gelfoam, and thrombin- soaked cottonoids. A dura matrix dural onlay substitute was placed. The bone
was reapproximated with a cranial plating system. The wound was then
copiously irrigated with antibiotic irrigation. The scalp was then reapproximated
in layers with 2-0 Vicryl sutures followed by a 4-0 Monocryl running suture. The
patient's hair was then washed with sterile water and chlorhexidine and dressed
with ChloraPrep solution and bacitracin ointment. The patient was removed from
Mayfield pin headholder. All counts were correct. There are no acute
complications.

Covid Test: Not needed, vaccinated
Nasal Ointment * A prescription for Bactroban (Mupirocin) Nasal Ointment will be sent to your pharmacy prior to surgery to
help prevent infection after surgery. * Use the Nasal Ointment 2 times per day (morning and night) for 5 days prior to surgery. * Put a pea size amount on a Q-Tip and swab inside each nostril. * If redness, irritation or medication allergy or intolerance of ointment occurs to notify their surgeon and stop
use of the ointment immediately. Shower
*A bottle of Dyna Hex Soap has been included in your packet. An infection after surgery can cause serious
problems with your recovery. Cleaning your skin before surgery with Dyna Hex Soap can lower your chance of
an infection.

Case 1832181 (RIGHT CRANIOTOMY FOR TUMOR) (continued) * Use your regular soap first. Shower with Dyna Hex Soap second. Leave on skin for 1 min before you rinse. * Keep Dyna Hex soap out of eyes, ears, nose, and mouth and away from genital area. * Stop using Dyna Hex Soap if you are allergic and switch to Dial antibacterial soap. * After cleaning with Dyna Hex Soap, rinse well with warm water & pat dry. * Always apply soap with a clean washcloth and dry off with a clean towel.
Fasting
*Do not eat any solid food 8 hours prior to your scheduled ARRIVAL time. Clear, see-through liquids 
(water, BLACK coffee, gatorade, ect.) are acceptable up until 2 hours prior to your scheduled ARRIVAL
time. No dairy (milk, creamer,shakes, ect.). Avoid candy, gum and mints. *Failure to follow these
instructions can lead to an increased risk of lung complications and may result in a delay or cancellation of your
procedure.
YOUR SCHEDULE:
5 Days Prior to Surgery
*Start Bactroban (mupirocin) Nasal Ointment. Once in the Morning & Once at Night. *Shower anytime with Dyna Hex Soap. Use clean washcloth and towel. 4 Days Prior to Surgery
*Bactroban (mupirocin) Nasal Ointment. Once in the Morning & Once at Night. *Shower anytime with Dyna Hex Soap. Use clean washcloth and towel. 3 Days Prior to Surgery
*Bactroban (mupirocin) Nasal Ointment. Once in the Morning & Once at Night. *Shower anytime with Dyna Hex Soap. Use clean washcloth and towel. 2 Days Prior to Surgery
*Bactroban (mupirocin) Nasal Ointment. Once in the Morning & Once at Night. *Shower anytime with Dyna Hex Soap. Use clean washcloth and towel. 1 Day Prior to Surgery
*Finish Bactroban (mupirocin) Nasal Ointment. Once in the Morning & Once at Night. *Shower at Night with Dyna Hex Soap. Use clean washcloth and towel. *Put on clean Pjs & sleep on clean sheets. *Do not smoke or chew tobacco after midnight. *Remove all jewelry (including wedding rings) & leave at home. Day of Surgery
*Shower right before leaving for the hospital with Dyna Hex Soap. Use clean washcloth & towel. *Do not use mascara, lotions, powder, make-up, perfume, or aftershave. *Bring CPAP, inhalers, glasses (no contacts), dentures & hearing aids (will be removed before surgery). *Don't wear jewelry and remove body piercing. *Bring picture ID, insurance card & copayment if needed. *Do not bring money or valuables, unless you've been told you have a co-pay. *Leave your luggage in the car. Your family will be responsible for your belongings. MEDICATION INSTRUCTIONS PER ANESTHESIA GUIDELINES:

Discharge Medications
· The nurses will give you a list of your new medications and home medication to resume. · A limited supply of pain medication will be provided at discharge. Take only as needed. Tylenol/acetaminophen may be taken in place of narcotic pain meds. Do not mix pain meds unless advised by
physician or nurse. Pain medication refills will only be considered by Dr. Sun after you have been seen on
your scheduled routine follow-up visit. · Prescription refills are completed during normal weekday office hours only. Please call the office at [PHONE-149] for:
**Do Not Use MyChart messaging for any post-op issues or needs, call the above number · A fever of greater than 101.5, measured with a thermometer. · Swelling, tenderness, redness or drainage from your incision. · Changes in level of awareness (restlessness, confusion, agitation, lethargy or increased sleepiness) · New speech or swallowing problems

· Changes in vision
· Persistent vomiting
· Severe headache, especially if worsening
· Seizures or tremors
· Leg swelling with calf tenderness

was performed. **Fatigue and lethargy are common after this procedure. This may last up to 6 weeks following surgery. **For further questions or concerns, please contact: · Kellie Kopp, RN, Patient Navigator [PHONE-150]

Main Entrance
Your To Do List:
Instructions for any of the following medications or any other blood thinners should be discussed with your 
neurosurgeon prior to surgery. · NSAIDS (Advil, Aleve, Motrin, Ibuprofen, Naproxen, Meloxicam, Diclofenac oral and gel, Celebrex or 
Aspirin) · Antiplatelet medications (Plavix and Brilinta) · Anticoagulation medications (Coumdain, Pradaxa, Eliquis, Xarelto, Lovenox) 
Covid Test: Not needed, vaccinated
Nasal Ointment * A prescription for Bactroban (Mupirocin) Nasal Ointment will be sent to your pharmacy prior to surgery to
help prevent infection after surgery. * Use the Nasal Ointment 2 times per day (morning and night) for 5 days prior to surgery. * Put a pea size amount on a Q-Tip and swab inside each nostril. * If redness, irritation or medication allergy or intolerance of ointment occurs to notify their surgeon and stop
use of the ointment immediately. Shower
*A bottle of Dyna Hex Soap has been included in your packet. An infection after surgery can cause serious
problems with your recovery. Cleaning your skin before surgery with Dyna Hex Soap can lower your chance of
an infection. * Use your regular soap first. Shower with Dyna Hex Soap second. Leave on skin for 1 min before you rinse. * Keep Dyna Hex soap out of eyes, ears, nose, and mouth and away from genital area. * Stop using Dyna Hex Soap if you are allergic and switch to Dial antibacterial soap. * After cleaning with Dyna Hex Soap, rinse well with warm water & pat dry. * Always apply soap with a clean washcloth and dry off with a clean towel.
Fasting
*Do not eat any solid food 8 hours prior to your scheduled ARRIVAL time. Clear, see-through liquids 
(water, BLACK coffee, gatorade, ect.) are acceptable up until 2 hours prior to your scheduled ARRIVAL
time. No dairy (milk, creamer,shakes, ect.). Avoid candy, gum and mints. *Failure to follow these
instructions can lead to an increased risk of lung complications and may result in a delay or cancellation of your
procedure.

Incision Care Wash your hair and gently massage the incision daily with baby shampoo. Do not use any creams or ointments. Do not blow dry, color or chemically treat your hair for at least 6 months. Discharge Activity Do not drive or operate dangerous
equipment within 24 hours of using pain meds. If you have had seizures, do not drive or operate dangerous equipment until cleared
by your surgeon. No lifting > 10 lbs. (i.e. one gallon of milk) or strenuous activity until cleared by your surgeon. Light walking is
encouraged. Discharge Diet Low sugar diet (No simple sugars, fruit juices, sweetened beverages, sweets made with sugar) while on
steroids. Daily multi-vitamin with minerals. Vitamin C supplement (500 mg daily for 30 days, 250 mg daily thereafter), if you are a
current or recent smoker. Discharge Medications The nurses will give you a list of your new medications and home medication to
resume. A limited supply of pain medication will be provided by your surgeon Take only as needed. Pain medication refills will only
be considered by your surgeon after you have been seen on your scheduled routine follow-up visit. I have counseled the patient on
the risks and benefits of narcotic use and patient has verbalized understanding. Prescription refills are completed during normal
weekday office hours only. Please call the office at [PHONE-270] for: A fever of greater than 101.5, measured with a
thermometer. Swelling, tenderness, redness or drainage from your incision. Changes in level of awareness (restlessness, confusion, agitation, lethargy or increased sleepiness) New speech or swallowing problems New weakness, especially one-sided Changes in
vision Persistent vomiting Severe headache, especially if worsening Seizures or tremors Leg swelling with calf tenderness If you think 
you are having an emergency, call 9-1-1. If possible, proceed to the hospital where your surgery was performed.

daily for 30 days, 250 mg daily thereafter), if you are a current or recent smoker. DISCHARGE MEDICATIONS - The nurses will give you a list of your new medications and home

[DOB-435] - Admission (Discharged) in NBH 3 West PCU (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Title: General Patient Education ()
Topic: Disease Management - PostOp General Surgery (Resolved)
Topic: Pain Management (Resolved)
Point: Incision/Wound Care (Resolved)
Know how to care for your wound. Emphasize good hand hygiene before and after caring for the the wound. Teach about signs and symptoms of infection and when to notify healthcare provider. Teach to tell family and friends to never touch wound or bandage and to clean their hands before and after visiting.
Instruct to keep incision/wound as clean and dry as possible. Caution against: scrubbing or rubbing the incision, removing the tape strips, using lotion or powder around the incision, exposing the incision to sunlight, taking a bath unless the incision can be kept dry.
Point: Pain Medication Actions & Side Effects (Resolved)
Encourage patient to drink plenty of fluids and to eat fruits and vegetables. Educate patient/family/caregiver to take pain medication with food to prevent nausea. Provide medication specific handouts when available.
Point: Discuss the Use of Pain Control Measures Before Pain Becomes Severe (Resolved)
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on how to care for incision/wound to include: how to clean, when to clean and any special
instruction for cleaning.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver that pain medication can cause constipation. Explain that a stool softener might need to be 
given while taking pain medication. Patient Friendly Description: -IV Pain Medication
Your nurse can call your doctor for an order and administer IV pain medication if indicated. This can be given through
your IV and lasts 1-2 hours. This may make you feel sleepy or dizzy. Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver that it is important to always let staff know if having difficulty breathing, pain or discomfort
before pain becomes severe.

[DOB-436] - Admission (Discharged) in NBH 3 West PCU (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Point: Explain Pain Rating Scale (Resolved)
Point: Non-Pharmacological Comfort Measures (Resolved)
Point: Patient Controlled Analgesia (Resolved)
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on the appropriate pain rating scale. Encourage patient/family/caregiver to monitor patient's 
pain.
Patient Friendly Description: -Your nurse will ask you to rate our pain on a scale of zero (0), for no pain, to ten (10), the
worst pain you can experience. -Your nurse will ask you to set a pain goal within zero (0) to ten (10) so that he or she can be sure that what we are doing
is working. -Mild pain is 1-3, Moderate pain is 4-6 and severe pain is 7-10. -We may not be able to take away ALL pain, so try to identify a point that pain would be manageable. -So if your pain goal is 4 or less and you are rating your pain at 7, your nurse would give you a pain medication and then
re-check your pain to ensure it is moving toward your pain goal of 4. Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Explain to patient/family/caregiver that there are other ways of controlling pain than medication. The following are
suggestions: position change, aromatherapy, deep slow breathing, distraction, quiet environment, imagery, heat therapy
and/or cold therapy, laughter, massage, music, physical therapy, and touch therapy. Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on the use of Patient Controlled Analgesia. Give the patient written information on Patient
Controlled Analgesia. Explain how the pump works. Demonstrate pushing the button to give pain medicine to the patient. Caution the patient and other family/visitors that only the patient should press the PCA button for pain relief to decrease the
chance of getting too much pain medicine. Learning Progress Summary

patient.
Patient Friendly Description: This is a procedure where an anesthesiologist or Certified Registered Nurse Anesthetist
(CRNA) will place a catheter in your back that provides continuous medication during your labor to keep you comfortable. -The anesthesiologist or CRNA will assess if you can have an epidural and will discuss risks of the procedure with you
prior to placement. -The epidural will make you feel numb from our waist down. It should take away sharp pain, but you will still feel pressure 
during labor. While pressure may be uncomfortable, it helps you know when to start pushing. Learning Progress Summary
